   - Result: Tie

- **Round 0 to Round 1 Transition**: 
  - Opponent played Scissors in Round 0 and then Paper in Round 1.
  - This is an "up" transition because Paper beats Rock (the move that would beat Scissors).

- **Round 1 to Round 2 Transition**:
  - Opponent played Paper in Round 1 and then Rock in Round 2.
  - This is a "down" transition because Rock loses to Paper.

**Hypothesis Refinement:**

- The opponent's transitions from Round 0 to Round 1 and Round 1 to Round 2 suggest a pattern of alternating between "up" and "down" transitions. This could indicate a strategy where the opponent is trying to predict my next move based on their previous move and adjust accordingly.

- Given the limited data, the opponent might be employing a strategy that involves alternating between moves that would beat their previous move and moves that would lose to their previous move. This could be a form of reactionary play where they are trying to anticipate my strategy.

**Counter Strategy:**

- If the opponent is alternating between "up" and "down" transitions, I can anticipate their next move by considering this pattern. After a "down" transition (Round 1 to Round 2), they might go for an "up" transition next.

- Therefore, if they follow this pattern, they might play Paper next (since Paper beats Rock, their last move).

- To counter this, I should play Scissors in the next round.

                There are three different kinds of transitions a player can make from their last round's move to their current move. 
                                    An up transition occurs when they play the move that would beat their last round's move. 
                                    A down transition occurs when they play the move that would lose to their last round's move. 
                                    A stay transition occurs when they play the move that is the same as their last round's move.
